<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>

<p><b>Robert Anthony De Niro</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/É/ 'a' in 'about'">É</span><span title="/Ë/ primary stress follows">Ë</span><span title="'n' in 'no'">n</span><span title="/Éªr/ 'irr' in 'mirror'">Éªr</span><span title="/oÊ/ long 'o' in 'code'">oÊ</span></span>/</a></span></span>; born August 17, 1943) is an American actor and producer who has both Italian and American citizenship.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-web.archive.org_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-web.archive.org-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-femalefirst.co.uk_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-femalefirst.co.uk-2">[2]</a></sup> He was cast as the young <a href="/wiki/Vito_Corleone" title="Vito Corleone">Vito Corleone</a> in the 1974 film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Godfather_Part_II" title="The Godfather Part II">The Godfather Part II</a></i>, for which he won the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actor" title="Academy Award for Best Supporting Actor">Academy Award for Best Supporting Actor</a>. His <a href="/wiki/Martin_Scorsese_and_Robert_De_Niro" title="Martin Scorsese and Robert De Niro">longtime collaboration</a> with director <a href="/wiki/Martin_Scorsese" title="Martin Scorsese">Martin Scorsese</a> earned him the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Actor" title="Academy Award for Best Actor">Academy Award for Best Actor</a> for his portrayal of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jake_La_Motta" title="Jake La Motta">Jake La Motta</a> in the 1980 film <i><a href="/wiki/Raging_Bull" title="Raging Bull">Raging Bull</a></i>. He received the <a href="/wiki/AFI_Life_Achievement_Award" title="AFI Life Achievement Award">AFI Life Achievement Award</a> in 2003, the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Cecil_B._DeMille_Award" title="Golden Globe Cecil B. DeMille Award">Golden Globe Cecil B. DeMille Award</a> in 2010, and the <a href="/wiki/Presidential_Medal_of_Freedom" title="Presidential Medal of Freedom">Presidential Medal of Freedom</a> from <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_United_States" title="President of the United States">President</a> <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> in 2016.</p>
<p>De Niro's first major film roles were in the sports drama, <i><a href="/wiki/Bang_the_Drum_Slowly_(film)" title="Bang the Drum Slowly (film)">Bang the Drum Slowly</a></i> (1973) and Scorsese's crime film <i><a href="/wiki/Mean_Streets" title="Mean Streets">Mean Streets</a></i> (1973). He earned <a href="/wiki/Academy_Awards" title="Academy Awards">Academy Award</a> nominations for the psychological thrillers <i><a href="/wiki/Taxi_Driver" title="Taxi Driver">Taxi Driver</a></i> (1976) and <i><a href="/wiki/Cape_Fear_(1991_film)" title="Cape Fear (1991 film)">Cape Fear</a></i> (1991), both directed by Scorsese. De Niro received additional nominations for <a href="/wiki/Michael_Cimino" title="Michael Cimino">Michael Cimino</a>'s Vietnam war drama, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Deer_Hunter" title="The Deer Hunter">The Deer Hunter</a></i> (1978), <a href="/wiki/Penny_Marshall" title="Penny Marshall">Penny Marshall</a>'s drama <i><a href="/wiki/Awakenings" title="Awakenings">Awakenings</a></i> (1990), and <a href="/wiki/David_O._Russell" title="David O. Russell">David O. Russell</a>'s romantic comedy-drama, <i><a href="/wiki/Silver_Linings_Playbook" title="Silver Linings Playbook">Silver Linings Playbook</a></i> (2012).</p>
<p>His portrayal of gangster <a href="/wiki/James_Burke_(gangster)" title="James Burke (gangster)">Jimmy Conway</a> in Scorsese's crime film, <i><a href="/wiki/Goodfellas" title="Goodfellas">Goodfellas</a></i> (1990), and his role in black comedy film <i><a href="/wiki/The_King_of_Comedy_(1983_film)" title="The King of Comedy (1983 film)">The King of Comedy</a></i> (1983), earned him <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_Film_Awards" title="British Academy Film Awards">BAFTA Award</a> nominations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup></p>
<p>De Niro has earned four nominations for the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Award_for_Best_Actor_%E2%80%93_Motion_Picture_Musical_or_Comedy" title="Golden Globe Award for Best Actor â Motion Picture Musical or Comedy">Golden Globe Award for Best Actor â Motion Picture Musical or Comedy</a>, for his work in the musical drama <i><a href="/wiki/New_York,_New_York_(1977_film)" title="New York, New York (1977 film)">New York, New York</a></i> (1977), the action comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Midnight_Run" title="Midnight Run">Midnight Run</a></i> (1988), the gangster comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Analyze_This" title="Analyze This">Analyze This</a></i> (1999), and the comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Meet_the_Parents" title="Meet the Parents">Meet the Parents</a></i> (2000). Other notable performances include roles in <i><a href="/wiki/Once_Upon_a_Time_in_America" title="Once Upon a Time in America">Once Upon a Time in America</a></i> (1984), <i><a href="/wiki/Brazil_(1985_film)" title="Brazil (1985 film)">Brazil</a></i> (1985), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Untouchables_(film)" title="The Untouchables (film)">The Untouchables</a></i> (1987), <i><a href="/wiki/Heat_(1995_film)" title="Heat (1995 film)">Heat</a></i> (1995), <i><a href="/wiki/Casino_(film)" title="Casino (film)">Casino</a></i> (1995), <i><a href="/wiki/Cop_Land" title="Cop Land">Cop Land</a></i> (1997), <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jackie_Brown_(film)" title="Jackie Brown (film)">Jackie Brown</a></i> (1997) and <i><a href="/wiki/Machete_(film)" title="Machete (film)">Machete</a></i> (2010). He has directed and starred in films such as the crime drama <i><a href="/wiki/A_Bronx_Tale" title="A Bronx Tale">A Bronx Tale</a></i> (1993), and the spy film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Good_Shepherd_(film)" title="The Good Shepherd (film)">The Good Shepherd</a></i> (2006).</p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Robert_De_Niro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Robert Anthony De Niro<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> was born in the <a href="/wiki/Greenwich_Village" title="Greenwich Village">Greenwich Village</a> area of <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>, New York, the son of <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Admiral" title="Virginia Admiral">Virginia Admiral</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_De_Niro_Sr." title="Robert De Niro Sr.">Robert De Niro Sr.</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vansha_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-vansha-5">[5]</a></sup> Both of his parents were painters;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vansha_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-vansha-5">[5]</a></sup> his father was of half <a href="/wiki/Italians" title="Italians">Italian</a> and half <a href="/wiki/Irish_people" title="Irish people">Irish</a> descent,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> while his mother was of half <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_people" title="German people">German</a> ancestry, with her other roots being <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">French</a>, <a href="/wiki/English_people" title="English people">English</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>De Niro's parents, who had met at the painting classes of <a href="/wiki/Hans_Hofmann" title="Hans Hofmann">Hans Hofmann</a> in <a href="/wiki/Provincetown,_Massachusetts" title="Provincetown, Massachusetts">Provincetown, Massachusetts</a>, divorced when he was two years old after his father announced that he was gay.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-8">[8]</a></sup> De Niro was raised by his mother in the Greenwich Village and <a href="/wiki/Little_Italy,_Manhattan" title="Little Italy, Manhattan">Little Italy</a> areas of Manhattan. His father lived within walking distance and De Niro spent much time with him as he grew up.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> His mother was raised <a href="/wiki/Presbyterianism" title="Presbyterianism">Presbyterian</a> but became an <a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">atheist</a> as an adult, while his father was a <a href="/wiki/Lapsed_Catholic" title="Lapsed Catholic">lapsed Catholic</a> since the age of 12.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-:1-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-10">[10]</a></sup> Against his parents' wishes, his grandparents had him secretly <a href="/wiki/Baptism" title="Baptism">baptized</a> into the Catholic Church while he was staying with them during his parents' divorce.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_8-2"><a href="#cite_note-:1-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>De Niro attended <a href="/wiki/List_of_public_elementary_schools_in_New_York_City#Region_9:_Manhattan.2C_the_Bronx" title="List of public elementary schools in New York City">PS 41</a>, a public elementary school in Manhattan, through the sixth grade. He then went to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Elisabeth_Irwin_High_School" title="Elisabeth Irwin High School">Elisabeth Irwin High School</a>, the private upper school of the <a href="/wiki/Little_Red_School_House" title="Little Red School House">Little Red School House</a>, for the seventh and eighth grades.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> He was accepted into the <a href="/wiki/Fiorello_H._LaGuardia_High_School" title="Fiorello H. LaGuardia High School">High School of Music and Art</a> for the ninth grade, but only attended for a short time before transferring to a public junior high school.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>De Niro began high school at the private <a href="/wiki/McBurney_School" title="McBurney School">McBurney School</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-baxter_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-baxter-13">[13]</a></sup> and later attended the private <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Preparatory_School" title="Rhodes Preparatory School">Rhodes Preparatory School</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> although he never graduated from either.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dougan.2C_pp._17-18_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dougan.2C_pp._17-18-15">[15]</a></sup> Nicknamed "Bobby Milk" for his pallor, De Niro hung out with a group of street kids as a youth in Little Italy, some of whom have remained his lifelong friends.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dougan.2C_p._17_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dougan.2C_p._17-16">[16]</a></sup> The direction of his future had already been foreshadowed by his stage debut at age 10, when he played the <a href="/wiki/Cowardly_Lion" title="Cowardly Lion">Cowardly Lion</a> in a school production of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wonderful_Wizard_of_Oz" title="The Wonderful Wizard of Oz">The Wizard of Oz</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tca_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-tca-17">[17]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Along with finding relief from shyness through performing, he was also fixated by cinema, and he dropped out of high school at age 16 to pursue acting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dougan.2C_p._17_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dougan.2C_p._17-16">[16]</a></sup> He studied acting at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stella_Adler_Conservatory" title="Stella Adler Conservatory">Stella Adler Conservatory</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Lee_Strasberg" title="Lee Strasberg">Lee Strasberg</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Actors_Studio" title="Actors Studio">Actors Studio</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dougan.2C_pp._17-18_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dougan.2C_pp._17-18-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>Robert De Niro received an Italian passport in 2006. His Italian citizenship was granted by the Prime Minister, on behalf of the Italian Republic despite a strong opposition of the American-Italian community <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-web.archive.org_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-web.archive.org-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-femalefirst.co.uk_2-1"><a href="#cite_note-femalefirst.co.uk-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career">Career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Robert_De_Niro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Acting_and_filmmaking">Acting and filmmaking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Robert_De_Niro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Acting and filmmaking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>De Niro's first film role came at the age of 20, when he appeared in <a href="/wiki/Brian_De_Palma" title="Brian De Palma">Brian De Palma</a>'s 1963 film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wedding_Party_(film)" title="The Wedding Party (film)">The Wedding Party</a></i>, but the film was not released until 1969. He then appeared in <a href="/wiki/Roger_Corman" title="Roger Corman">Roger Corman</a>'s film <i><a href="/wiki/Bloody_Mama" title="Bloody Mama">Bloody Mama</a></i> (1970). He gained popular attention with his role as a dying <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> player in <i><a href="/wiki/Bang_the_Drum_Slowly_(film)" title="Bang the Drum Slowly (film)">Bang the Drum Slowly</a></i> (1973) and began his collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Martin_Scorsese" title="Martin Scorsese">Martin Scorsese</a> when he played the small-time criminal Johnny Boy in <i><a href="/wiki/Mean_Streets" title="Mean Streets">Mean Streets</a></i> (1973).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tca_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-tca-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>De Niro had a pivotal role in the <a href="/wiki/Francis_Ford_Coppola" title="Francis Ford Coppola">Francis Ford Coppola</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Godfather_Part_II" title="The Godfather Part II">The Godfather Part II</a></i> (1974), playing the young <a href="/wiki/Vito_Corleone" title="Vito Corleone">Vito Corleone</a>. Coppola had remembered his previous auditions for the roles of <a href="/wiki/Sonny_Corleone" title="Sonny Corleone">Sonny Corleone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Corleone" title="Michael Corleone">Michael Corleone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carlo_Rizzi_(The_Godfather)" title="Carlo Rizzi (The Godfather)">Carlo Rizzi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Paulie_Gatto_(The_Godfather)" title="Paulie Gatto (The Godfather)">Paulie Gatto</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Godfather" title="The Godfather">The Godfather</a></i>. His performance earned him his first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a>, for <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actor" title="Academy Award for Best Supporting Actor">Best Supporting Actor</a>, although Coppola accepted the award as De Niro was not present at the ceremony. De Niro became the first actor to win an Academy Award speaking mainly a foreign language. In this case, several <a href="/wiki/Sicilian_language" title="Sicilian language">Sicilian</a> dialects,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tca_17-2"><a href="#cite_note-tca-17">[17]</a></sup> although he delivered a few lines in English. He and <a href="/wiki/Marlon_Brando" title="Marlon Brando">Marlon Brando</a>, who played the older Vito Corleone in the first film, are the only actors to have won Oscars for portraying the same fictional character.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> After working with Scorsese in <i>Mean Streets</i>, De Niro went on to have a successful working relationship with him in films such as <i><a href="/wiki/Taxi_Driver" title="Taxi Driver">Taxi Driver</a></i> (1976), <i><a href="/wiki/New_York,_New_York_(1977_film)" title="New York, New York (1977 film)">New York, New York</a></i> (1977), <i><a href="/wiki/Raging_Bull" title="Raging Bull">Raging Bull</a></i> (1980), <i><a href="/wiki/The_King_of_Comedy_(1983_film)" title="The King of Comedy (1983 film)">The King of Comedy</a></i> (1983), <i><a href="/wiki/Goodfellas" title="Goodfellas">Goodfellas</a></i> (1990), <i><a href="/wiki/Cape_Fear_(1991_film)" title="Cape Fear (1991 film)">Cape Fear</a></i> (1991), and <i><a href="/wiki/Casino_(film)" title="Casino (film)">Casino</a></i> (1995). They also acted together in <i><a href="/wiki/Guilty_by_Suspicion" title="Guilty by Suspicion">Guilty by Suspicion</a></i> (1991) and provided their voices for the animated feature <i><a href="/wiki/Shark_Tale" title="Shark Tale">Shark Tale</a></i> (2004). <i>Taxi Driver</i> was particularly important to De Niro's career. His iconic performance as <a href="/wiki/Travis_Bickle" title="Travis Bickle">Travis Bickle</a> catapulted him to stardom and forever linked his name with Bickle's famous "<a href="/wiki/Taxi_Driver#.22You_talkin.27_to_me.3F.22" title="Taxi Driver">You talkin' to me?</a>" monologue, which De Niro largely improvised.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> The role of Bickle earned him his first Academy Award Nomination for Best Actor. His portrayal of <a href="/wiki/Jake_LaMotta" title="Jake LaMotta">Jake LaMotta</a> in <i>Raging Bull</i> was lauded, as well as his interpretation of <a href="/wiki/Max_Cady" title="Max Cady">Max Cady</a> in <i>Cape Fear</i>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RobertdeNiro26.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3483" data-file-width="2476" height="309" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/RobertdeNiro26.JPG/220px-RobertdeNiro26.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/RobertdeNiro26.JPG/330px-RobertdeNiro26.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ef/RobertdeNiro26.JPG/440px-RobertdeNiro26.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RobertdeNiro26.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
De Niro in 1988</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1976, De Niro appeared in <i><a href="/wiki/1900_(film)" title="1900 (film)">1900</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Bernardo_Bertolucci" title="Bernardo Bertolucci">Bernardo Bertolucci</a>'s biographical exploration of life in Italy before <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, seen through the eyes of two Italian childhood friends at the opposite sides of society's hierarchy. He also starred in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Last_Tycoon_(1976_film)" title="The Last Tycoon (1976 film)">The Last Tycoon</a></i> (1976), directed by <a href="/wiki/Elia_Kazan" title="Elia Kazan">Elia Kazan</a>. Kazan recalls that De Niro "would do almost anything to succeed" and noted that he cut his weight down from 170 to 128 pounds for the role in this film. Kazan adds that De Niro "is one of a select number of actors I've directed who work hard at their trade, and the only one who asked to rehearse on Sundays. Most of the others play tennis. Bobby and I would go over the scenes to be shot. Bobby is more meticulous... he's very imaginative. He's very precise. He figures everything out both inside and outside. He has good emotion. He's a <a href="/wiki/Character_actor" title="Character actor">character actor</a>: everything he does he calculates. In a good way, but he calculates."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kazan_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kazan-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:766</sup> Kazan developed and used those personality traits for his character in the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kazan_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kazan-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:766</sup> And although the film did poorly at the box office, reviewers praised De Niro's acting. Film critic Marie Brenner wrote that "for De Niro, it is a role that surpasses even his brilliant and daring portrayal of Vito Corleone in <i>The Godfather Part II</i>... his performance deserves to be compared with the very finest".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> De Niro played Michael Vronsky in the acclaimed Vietnam War film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Deer_Hunter" title="The Deer Hunter">The Deer Hunter</a></i> (1978), for which he was nominated for Best Actor in a Leading Role. Fearing he had become typecast in <a href="/wiki/Mafia" title="Mafia">mob</a> roles, he began expanding into occasional comedic roles in the mid-1980s and has had much success there as well, with such films as <i><a href="/wiki/Brazil_(1985_film)" title="Brazil (1985 film)">Brazil</a></i> (1985), <i><a href="/wiki/Midnight_Run" title="Midnight Run">Midnight Run</a></i> (1988), <i><a href="/wiki/Analyze_This" title="Analyze This">Analyze This</a></i> (1999), <i><a href="/wiki/Meet_the_Parents" title="Meet the Parents">Meet the Parents</a></i> (2000), and <i><a href="/wiki/Meet_the_Fockers" title="Meet the Fockers">Meet the Fockers</a></i> (2004). Other films include <i><a href="/wiki/True_Confessions_(film)" title="True Confessions (film)">True Confessions</a></i> (1981), <i><a href="/wiki/Falling_in_Love_(1984_film)" title="Falling in Love (1984 film)">Falling in Love</a></i> (1984), <i><a href="/wiki/Once_Upon_a_Time_in_America" title="Once Upon a Time in America">Once Upon a Time in America</a></i> (1984), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mission_(1986_film)" title="The Mission (1986 film)">The Mission</a></i> (1986), <i><a href="/wiki/Angel_Heart" title="Angel Heart">Angel Heart</a></i> (1987), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Untouchables_(film)" title="The Untouchables (film)">The Untouchables</a></i> (1987), <i><a href="/wiki/Goodfellas" title="Goodfellas">Goodfellas</a></i> (1990), <i><a href="/wiki/Awakenings" title="Awakenings">Awakenings</a></i> (1990), <i><a href="/wiki/Heat_(1995_film)" title="Heat (1995 film)">Heat</a></i> (1995), <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fan_(1996_film)" title="The Fan (1996 film)">The Fan</a></i> (1996), <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sleepers_(film)" title="Sleepers (film)">Sleepers</a></i> (1996), <i><a href="/wiki/Wag_the_Dog" title="Wag the Dog">Wag the Dog</a></i> (1997), <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jackie_Brown_(film)" title="Jackie Brown (film)">Jackie Brown</a></i> (1997), <i><a href="/wiki/Ronin_(film)" title="Ronin (film)">Ronin</a></i> (1998) and <i><a href="/wiki/Flawless_(1999_film)" title="Flawless (1999 film)">Flawless</a></i> (1999).</p>
<p>In 1987, De Niro was the President of the Jury at the <a href="/wiki/15th_Moscow_International_Film_Festival" title="15th Moscow International Film Festival">15th Moscow International Film Festival</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moscow1987_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-Moscow1987-22">[22]</a></sup> He appeared in <i><a href="/wiki/This_Boy%27s_Life_(film)" title="This Boy's Life (film)">This Boy's Life</a></i> (1993). Around this time, he was offered the role of Mitch Leary in <i><a href="/wiki/In_the_Line_of_Fire" title="In the Line of Fire">In the Line of Fire</a></i> (1993). However, due to scheduling conflicts with his directorial debut <i><a href="/wiki/A_Bronx_Tale" title="A Bronx Tale">A Bronx Tale</a></i> (1993), he gave up the role to <a href="/wiki/John_Malkovich" title="John Malkovich">John Malkovich</a>, who later received an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> nomination for it. In <i>A Bronx Tale</i>, which De Niro agreed to direct after seeing the screenwriter's one-man <a href="/wiki/Off-Broadway" title="Off-Broadway">off-Broadway</a> play, he played a bus driver who struggles to keep his son away from a local mobster. At the <a href="/wiki/20th_Moscow_International_Film_Festival" title="20th Moscow International Film Festival">20th Moscow International Film Festival</a> in 1997, he was awarded an Honorable Prize for contribution to cinema.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Moscow1997_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-Moscow1997-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Robert_De_Niro_2011_Shankbone.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3843" data-file-width="2803" height="302" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Robert_De_Niro_2011_Shankbone.JPG/220px-Robert_De_Niro_2011_Shankbone.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Robert_De_Niro_2011_Shankbone.JPG/330px-Robert_De_Niro_2011_Shankbone.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/01/Robert_De_Niro_2011_Shankbone.JPG/440px-Robert_De_Niro_2011_Shankbone.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">

De Niro at the <a href="/wiki/Tribeca_Film_Festival" title="Tribeca Film Festival">Tribeca Film Festival</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>De Niro would reference <i>In the Line of Fire</i>, along with <i><a href="/wiki/Dirty_Harry" title="Dirty Harry">Dirty Harry</a></i> (1971) and <i><a href="/wiki/Magnum_Force" title="Magnum Force">Magnum Force</a></i> (1973), two more of Eastwood's films, in <i><a href="/wiki/Righteous_Kill" title="Righteous Kill">Righteous Kill</a></i> (2008). He also appeared in the crime drama <i><a href="/wiki/Cop_Land" title="Cop Land">Cop Land</a></i> (1997). He starred in the police action-thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Heat_(1995_film)" title="Heat (1995 film)">Heat</a></i> (1995), along with fellow actor and long-time friend, <a href="/wiki/Al_Pacino" title="Al Pacino">Al Pacino</a>. The duo drew much attention from fans, as both have generally been compared throughout their careers. Though Pacino and De Niro both starred in <i>The Godfather Part II</i> (1974), they shared no screen time. They once again appeared together in <i>Righteous Kill</i> (2008).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>De Niro played Master Chief Billy Sunday in the biographical film <i><a href="/wiki/Men_of_Honor" title="Men of Honor">Men of Honor</a></i> (2000), based on the life of <a href="/wiki/Carl_Brashear" title="Carl Brashear">Carl Brashear</a>, the first African American to become a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Master_Diver_(United_States_Navy)" title="Master Diver (United States Navy)">U.S. Navy Master Diver</a>. He also hosted <i><a href="/wiki/9/11_(film)" title="9/11 (film)">9/11</a></i> (2002), a documentary about the <a href="/wiki/September_11_attacks" title="September 11 attacks">9/11 attacks</a>, shown on <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> and focusing on video footage made by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jules_and_Gedeon_Naudet" title="Jules and Gedeon Naudet">Jules and Gedeon Naudet</a> that showed the role of firefighters following the attacks. He reprised his role as Jack Byrnes in <i><a href="/wiki/Meet_the_Fockers" title="Meet the Fockers">Meet the Fockers</a></i> (2004) and was featured in <i><a href="/wiki/Stardust_(2007_film)" title="Stardust (2007 film)">Stardust</a></i> (2007). All of the films were successful at the box office, but received mixed reviews.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Robert_De_Niro_2011_2.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4608" data-file-width="3072" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Robert_De_Niro_2011_2.JPG/170px-Robert_De_Niro_2011_2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Robert_De_Niro_2011_2.JPG/255px-Robert_De_Niro_2011_2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Robert_De_Niro_2011_2.JPG/340px-Robert_De_Niro_2011_2.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Robert_De_Niro_2011_2.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
De Niro in 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>De Niro had to turn down a role in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Departed" title="The Departed">The Departed</a></i> (2006) due to commitments with preparing <i><a href="/wiki/The_Good_Shepherd_(film)" title="The Good Shepherd (film)">The Good Shepherd</a></i> (2006). He said: "I wanted to. I wish I could've been able to, but I was preparing <i>The Good Shepherd</i> so much that I couldn't take the time to. I was trying to figure a way to do it while I was preparing. It just didn't seem possible."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tfdeniro_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-tfdeniro-25">[25]</a></sup> In June 2006, it was announced that De Niro had donated his film archive (including scripts, costumes, and props) to the <a href="/wiki/Harry_Ransom_Center" title="Harry Ransom Center">Harry Ransom Center</a> at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Texas_at_Austin" title="University of Texas at Austin">University of Texas at Austin</a>. On April 27, 2009, it was announced that the De Niro collection at the Ransom Center was open to researchers and the public. De Niro directed and starred in <i>The Good Shepherd</i> (2006). The film reunited him onscreen with <a href="/wiki/Joe_Pesci" title="Joe Pesci">Joe Pesci</a>, with whom he had starred in <i>Raging Bull</i>, <i>Goodfellas</i>, <i>A Bronx Tale</i>, <i>Once Upon a Time in America</i>, and <i>Casino</i>. De Niro announced that he would appear in the <a href="/wiki/Edge_of_Darkness_(2010_film)" title="Edge of Darkness (2010 film)">film version</a> of the BBC crime series <i><a href="/wiki/Edge_of_Darkness" title="Edge of Darkness">Edge of Darkness</a></i> in 2010. However, just after he arrived to begin shooting, De Niro left the film due to creative differences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> He was replaced by <a href="/wiki/Ray_Winstone" title="Ray Winstone">Ray Winstone</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> He appeared as Senator John McLaughlin in the action film <i><a href="/wiki/Machete_(film)" title="Machete (film)">Machete</a></i> (2010), and starred in the thriller <i><a href="/wiki/Stone_(2010_film)" title="Stone (2010 film)">Stone</a></i> (2010). He again reprised his role as Jack Byrnes in <i><a href="/wiki/Little_Fockers" title="Little Fockers">Little Fockers</a></i> (2010). He appeared in the action film <i><a href="/wiki/Killer_Elite_(film)" title="Killer Elite (film)">Killer Elite</a></i> (2011), <i><a href="/wiki/Limitless_(film)" title="Limitless (film)">Limitless</a></i> (2011) and the romantic comedy film <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Eve_(film)" title="New Year's Eve (film)">New Year's Eve</a></i> (2011).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-imdb.com_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-imdb.com-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>De Niro starred in the film <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Manuale_d%27amore_3" title="Manuale d'amore 3">Manuale d'amore 3</a></i> (2011).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> In January 2011, <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> picked up De Niro's crime pilot, <i><a href="/wiki/NYC_22" title="NYC 22">NYC 22</a></i> (originally titled <i>Rookies</i>), but it was cancelled after airing only four episodes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> In 2011, De Niro was the President of the Jury for the 64th Cannes Film Festival.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> In 2012, he starred in the films <i><a href="/wiki/Silver_Linings_Playbook" title="Silver Linings Playbook">Silver Linings Playbook</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Freelancers_(film)" title="Freelancers (film)">Freelancers</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Red_Lights_(2012_film)" title="Red Lights (2012 film)">Red Lights</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Being_Flynn" title="Being Flynn">Being Flynn</a></i>. He received a nomination for an <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Supporting_Actor" title="Academy Award for Best Supporting Actor">Academy Award for Best Supporting Actor</a> for his role in <i>Silver Linings Playbook</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup></p>
<p>On April 8, 2015, De Niro revealed that he'll play <a href="/wiki/Enzo_Ferrari" title="Enzo Ferrari">Enzo Ferrari</a> in a movie to be released in 2016.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_work">Other work</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Robert_De_Niro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Other work">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>De Niro's capital ventures have included co-founding the film studio <a href="/wiki/TriBeCa_Productions" title="TriBeCa Productions">TriBeCa Productions</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Tribeca_Film_Festival" title="Tribeca Film Festival">Tribeca Film Festival</a>, the restaurants <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nobu" title="Nobu">Nobu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tribeca_Grill" title="Tribeca Grill">Tribeca Grill</a> (which he co-owns with Broadway producer <a href="/wiki/Stewart_F._Lane" title="Stewart F. Lane">Stewart F. Lane</a>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> The Greenwich Hotel (located in Tribeca),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> and the restaurant inside the hotel, Locanda Verde (run by executive chef and co-owner <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Carmellini" title="Andrew Carmellini">Andrew Carmellini</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> According to the July 2010 issue of <i>Gourmet</i> magazine, De Niro is in negotiations with an internationally renowned chef, Natalia Jibladze, to launch an as-yet-unnamed restaurant in Manhattan under his Tribeca trademark. When in <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">Malaysia</a> in 2010, he dined with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Malaysian_Prime_Minister" title="Malaysian Prime Minister">Malaysian Prime Minister</a>'s wife and was asked to open a Malay restaurant in <a href="/wiki/Alor_Setar" title="Alor Setar">Alor Setar</a>, Kedah.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Acting_style_and_legacy">Acting style and legacy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Robert_De_Niro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Acting style and legacy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:RobertDeNiroTCLChineseTheatreJan2013.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="808" data-file-width="1005" height="177" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/RobertDeNiroTCLChineseTheatreJan2013.jpg/220px-RobertDeNiroTCLChineseTheatreJan2013.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/RobertDeNiroTCLChineseTheatreJan2013.jpg/330px-RobertDeNiroTCLChineseTheatreJan2013.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/RobertDeNiroTCLChineseTheatreJan2013.jpg/440px-RobertDeNiroTCLChineseTheatreJan2013.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:RobertDeNiroTCLChineseTheatreJan2013.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
De Niro having his hand- and shoe-prints placed in cement at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TCL_Chinese_Theatre" title="TCL Chinese Theatre">TCL Chinese Theatre</a> in February 2013</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>De Niro studied with <a href="/wiki/Stella_Adler" title="Stella Adler">Stella Adler</a> where he learned the techniques of the Stanislavski-system. He is praised for his commitment to roles, De Niro gained 60Â lb (27Â kg) and learned how to <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">box</a> for his role as <a href="/wiki/Jake_LaMotta" title="Jake LaMotta">Jake LaMotta</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/Raging_Bull" title="Raging Bull">Raging Bull</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tca_17-3"><a href="#cite_note-tca-17">[17]</a></sup> ground his teeth for <i><a href="/wiki/Cape_Fear_(1991_film)" title="Cape Fear (1991 film)">Cape Fear</a></i>, lived in <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a> for <i><a href="/wiki/The_Godfather_Part_II" title="The Godfather Part II">The Godfather Part II</a></i>, worked as a cab driver for a few weeks for <i><a href="/wiki/Taxi_Driver" title="Taxi Driver">Taxi Driver</a></i>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> and learned to play the saxophone for <i><a href="/wiki/New_York,_New_York_(1977_film)" title="New York, New York (1977 film)">New York, New York</a></i>. He again put on weight for his performance as <a href="/wiki/Al_Capone" title="Al Capone">Al Capone</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Untouchables_(film)" title="The Untouchables (film)">The Untouchables</a></i> (1987).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>De Niro's brand of acting includes employing whatever extreme tactic he feels is necessary to elicit the best performance from those with whom he is working. During the filming of <i><a href="/wiki/The_King_of_Comedy_(1983_film)" title="The King of Comedy (1983 film)">The King of Comedy</a></i>, he directed a slew of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anti-Semitic" title="Anti-Semitic">anti-Semitic</a> epithets at co-star <a href="/wiki/Jerry_Lewis" title="Jerry Lewis">Jerry Lewis</a> to enhance and authenticate the anger demonstrated by Lewis' character. According to <a href="/wiki/People_(magazine)" title="People (magazine)"><i>People</i></a> magazine, the technique was successful, with Lewis recalling: "I forgot the cameras were there... I was going for Bobby's throat."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Robert_De_Niro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Family">Family</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Robert_De_Niro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Family">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>De Niro married his first wife, <a href="/wiki/Diahnne_Abbott" title="Diahnne Abbott">Diahnne Abbott</a>, in 1976. They have a son, Raphael, a former actor who works in New York real estate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> De Niro also adopted Abbott's daughter <a href="/wiki/Drena_De_Niro" title="Drena De Niro">Drena De Niro</a> from a previous relationship. They divorced in 1988. De Niro has twin sons Aaron Kendrick and Julian Henry de Niro conceived by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/In_vitro_fertilization" title="In vitro fertilization"><i>in vitro</i> fertilization</a> and delivered by a surrogate mother in 1995, from a long relationship with former model <a href="/wiki/Toukie_Smith" title="Toukie Smith">Toukie Smith</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Robert_De_Niro_Cannes_2016_5.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="800" data-file-width="354" height="497" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Robert_De_Niro_Cannes_2016_5.jpg/220px-Robert_De_Niro_Cannes_2016_5.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Robert_De_Niro_Cannes_2016_5.jpg/330px-Robert_De_Niro_Cannes_2016_5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/0/05/Robert_De_Niro_Cannes_2016_5.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Robert_De_Niro_Cannes_2016_5.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
De Niro and wife <a href="/wiki/Grace_Hightower" title="Grace Hightower">Grace Hightower</a> in 2016</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1997, De Niro married his second wife, actress <a href="/wiki/Grace_Hightower" title="Grace Hightower">Grace Hightower</a>, at their <a href="/wiki/Marbletown,_New_York" title="Marbletown, New York">Marbletown</a> home.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Custody_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-Custody-45">[45]</a></sup> Their son Elliot was born in 1998 and the couple split in 1999. The divorce was never finalized and in 2004 they renewed their vows.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Custody_45-1"><a href="#cite_note-Custody-45">[45]</a></sup> In December 2011, a daughter named Helen Grace was born via surrogate.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> In addition to his six children, De Niro has four grandchildren, one from his daughter Drena and three from his son Raphael.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<p>De Niro announced on March 25, 2016 that his son, Elliot, has <a href="/wiki/Autism" title="Autism">autism</a> and explained his interest in its causes and treatment.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>It was reported in October 2003 that De Niro had been diagnosed with <a href="/wiki/Prostate_cancer" title="Prostate cancer">prostate cancer</a>. He underwent surgery at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Memorial_Sloan-Kettering_Cancer_Center" title="Memorial Sloan-Kettering Cancer Center">Memorial Sloan-Kettering Cancer Center</a> in December 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Properties">Properties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Robert_De_Niro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Properties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>De Niro, who has long resided in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>, has been investing in <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">Manhattan</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Tribeca" title="Tribeca">Tribeca</a> neighborhood since 1989. He has residences on the <a href="/wiki/East_Side_(Manhattan)" title="East Side (Manhattan)">east</a> and <a href="/wiki/West_Side_(Manhattan)" title="West Side (Manhattan)">west sides</a> of Manhattan. He also has a 78-acre (32Â ha) estate in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gardiner_(town),_New_York" title="Gardiner (town), New York">Gardiner, New York</a>, which serves as his primary residence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gardiner_lawsuit_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gardiner_lawsuit-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legal_issues">Legal issues</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Robert_De_Niro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Legal issues">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During a film shoot in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> in February 1998, De Niro was questioned as a witness about the Bourgeois prostitution ring.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> De Niro denied any involvement,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbcfurious_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbcfurious-56">[56]</a></sup> later filing a complaint.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Despite saying at the time that he would not return to France, he later filmed there and presided over the jury at the <a href="/wiki/2011_Cannes_Film_Festival" title="2011 Cannes Film Festival">2011 Cannes Film Festival</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2006, the <a href="/wiki/Land_trust" title="Land trust">trust</a> that owns De Niro's Gardiner estate sued the town to have its <a href="/wiki/Property_tax" title="Property tax">property tax</a> <a href="/wiki/Tax_assessment" title="Tax assessment">assessment</a> reduced, arguing that, at $6 million, it was too high and should be compared only with similar properties in <a href="/wiki/Ulster_County,_New_York" title="Ulster County, New York">Ulster County</a>, where Gardiner is located. The town, which had been comparing its value to similar estates in <a href="/wiki/Dutchess_County,_New_York" title="Dutchess County, New York">Dutchess County</a>, across the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">Hudson River</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Connecticut" title="Connecticut">Connecticut</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Litchfield_County,_Connecticut" title="Litchfield County, Connecticut">Litchfield County</a>, east of Dutchess, where many other wealthy New York City residents maintain estates on large properties, won in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_York_State_Supreme_Court" title="New York State Supreme Court">State Supreme Court</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NY_Times_Gardiner_story_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-NY_Times_Gardiner_story-59">[59]</a></sup> But in 2014, the trust's lawyers appealed the decision and the town was unsure if it should continue to defend the suit because of its own financial limitations (it would have earned far less in payments on the increased taxes than it had spent in legal bills). This has made many residents, who initially sympathized with De Niro, angry, and some proposed to raise money privately to help the town continue the suit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gardiner_lawsuit_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gardiner_lawsuit-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<p>A local newspaper's report on the continued dispute was picked up by <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> and made international news. "When he read about it on <a href="/wiki/Election_Day_(United_States)" title="Election Day (United States)">Election Day</a>, he went bananas," due to the negative publicity, said Gardiner town councilman Wiegand. He had apparently been unaware that the trust had filed the lawsuit. Its accountants took the blame, citing their <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fiduciary_duty" title="Fiduciary duty">fiduciary duty</a>. A short time later, his lawyer met with town officials, at De Niro's direction, and offered them withdrawal of the suit and $129,000 in reimbursement for the town's legal bills, paid by the accounting firm.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT_Gardiner_settlement_story_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT_Gardiner_settlement_story-60">[60]</a></sup> "[He] made it very clear that De Niro didn't want to screw the town, that he didn't know about any of it and that he wanted it settled as quickly as possible," Wiegand said.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gardiner_settlement_61-0"><a href="#cite_note-Gardiner_settlement-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_activism">Political activism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Robert_De_Niro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Political activism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1998, he lobbied Congress against impeaching President <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<p>While promoting the film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Good_Shepherd_(film)" title="The Good Shepherd (film)">The Good Shepherd</a></i> with co-star <a href="/wiki/Matt_Damon" title="Matt Damon">Matt Damon</a> on the December 8, 2006, episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Hardball_with_Chris_Matthews" title="Hardball with Chris Matthews">Hardball with Chris Matthews</a></i> at <a href="/wiki/George_Mason_University" title="George Mason University">George Mason University</a>, De Niro was asked whom he would like to see as President of the United States. De Niro responded, "Well, I think of two people: <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">Hillary Clinton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Obama</a>."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> On February 4, 2008, De Niro supported Obama at a rally at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Izod_Center" title="Izod Center">Izod Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a> before <a href="/wiki/Super_Tuesday" title="Super Tuesday">Super Tuesday</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2012, De Niro joined the anti fracking campaign <a href="/wiki/Artists_Against_Fracking" title="Artists Against Fracking">Artists Against Fracking</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_2016" title="United States presidential election, 2016">2016 presidential campaign</a>, De Niro was an outspoken critic of candidate <a href="/wiki/Donald_Trump" title="Donald Trump">Donald Trump</a>, calling him "so blatantly stupid" and stating "I'd like to punch him in the face" in reference to the similar desire Trump expressed towards the DNC speakers at one of his rallies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_views">Religious views</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Robert_De_Niro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Religious views">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>De Niro was raised by an atheist mother and a <a href="/wiki/Lapsed_Catholic" title="Lapsed Catholic">lapsed Catholic</a> father who left the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a> at age 12.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-:1-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-:2-10">[10]</a></sup> His grandparents had him secretly <a href="/wiki/Baptism" title="Baptism">baptized</a> Catholic, and his grandmother was the main advocate of Catholicism in the family.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> He refuses to be asked about religion in interviews.</p>
<p>When asked why he would not play <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Jesus Christ</a> in <a href="/wiki/Martin_Scorsese" title="Martin Scorsese">Martin Scorsese</a>'s 1988 film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Last_Temptation_of_Christ_(film)" title="The Last Temptation of Christ (film)">The Last Temptation of Christ</a></i>, he explained on at least two different occasions:</p>
<blockquote>
<p><i>Last Temptation</i> was something I was never interested in doing. But I did tell [Scorsese], 'If you really have a problem, if you really want to do it, and you need me, I'll do it. If you're against the wall and have no other way, I'll do it as a friend.'<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_8-4"><a href="#cite_note-:1-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_10-3"><a href="#cite_note-:2-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<blockquote>
<p>I was not interested in playing Christ. It's like playing <a href="/wiki/Prince_Hamlet" title="Prince Hamlet">Hamlet</a>. I just didn't want to do it. Marty and I talked about it. We do things with each other because we like to work together, but also for our separate reasons. I have mine as an actor, he has his as a director. That's the best way.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_10-4"><a href="#cite_note-:2-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
</blockquote>
<p>In addition, De Niro has played a number of Catholic characters in his movies. He played a Catholic penitent in the 1986 film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Mission_(1986_film)" title="The Mission (1986 film)">The Mission</a></i>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Anti-vaccination_movement">Anti-vaccination movement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Robert_De_Niro&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Anti-vaccination movement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>De Niro initially supported the inclusion of the controversial documentary about an alleged vaccination coverup, <i><a href="/wiki/Vaxxed" title="Vaxxed">Vaxxed</a></i>, at the 2016 <a href="/wiki/Tribeca_Film_Festival" title="Tribeca Film Festival">Tribeca Film Festival</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian2016_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian2016-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HRoffit_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-HRoffit-70">[70]</a></sup> He explained his interest in the film resulted from his family experience with an autistic son.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian2016_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian2016-69">[69]</a></sup> De Niro withdrew his recommendation after discussion with the scientific community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian2016_69-2"><a href="#cite_note-Guardian2016-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> He said he was pressured by some festival filmmakers to remove <i>Vaxxed</i> from the festival line-up. He also said that he intends to be a part of the conversation around vaccines and autism in the future.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> The director of the film, <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Wakefield" title="Andrew Wakefield">Andrew Wakefield</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HRoffit_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-HRoffit-70">[70]</a></sup> who is considered the father of the anti-vaccination movement,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-awnw_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-awnw-73">[73]</a></sup> had reportedly been communicating with Grace Hightower and in one reported exchange sympathized with them saying: "your family's life [has] been blighted by autism".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-lbrb_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-lbrb-74">[74]</a></sup></p>

<th class="navbox-group" scope="row">(2001â2009)</th>
